In criminal investigations, communications that discuss only fictional or hypothetical scenarios are generally considered irrelevant unless they can be shown to have a direct nexus to actual conduct.\n\n3. **Relevance Test (U.S. Evidence Rules / Common Law)**  \n   Under the most widely applied relevance standard (e.g., U.S. Federal Rule of Evidence 401), evidence must \u201chave any tendency to make the existence of any fact that is of importance to the determination of the action more probable or less probable.\u201d  \n   - The chat does not make any fact (e.g., that Alex is actually selling drugs) more or less probable.  \n   - The only potentially pertinent fact it could touch is Alex\u2019s *state of mind* or *predisposition*, but that is a very weak link and would normally be excluded as character evidence under Rule 404(b) unless it is essential to a specific claim (e.g., intent or motive) and is admissible in a manner that limits its probative value.\n\n4. **Potentially Excludable Character Evidence**  \n   Even if a prosecutor argued that the chat demonstrates Alex\u2019s \u201cwillingness to use drugs\u201d or a \u201cdesire for power,\u201d such character evidence is typically inadmissible to prove conduct in this case. Courts usually exclude it unless the defendant has established that the alleged character trait is essential to a particular element of the offense (e.g., intent to distribute). The chat does not meet that threshold.\n\n5. **Lack of Corroborating Evidence**  \n   An investigator would need additional evidence that connects Alex\u2019s words to actual activity (e.g., a subsequent text about a real meeting, a phone call about a drug sale, or possession of paraphernalia). In the absence of such corroboration, the chat alone cannot establish Alex\u2019s involvement.\n\n**Bottom line:**  \nThe chat is a discussion of a fictional series with no concrete references to real drug dealing. The court would almost certainly exclude it. |\n| **Character evidence** | The chat could be construed as character evidence (\u201cAlex is the kind of person who thinks about cooking meth\u201d).
